[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] advisor.started
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] The
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  worker is heading toward a 2^60 brute force (the
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  triple nested K3/K2/K1 loop), which will not finish in 120s. There is a much better structure to exploit.
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  Stop and rethink the math.

Key insight you already have
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] : **F is invertible**, and each round key enters as `F(R
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  ⊕ K)`. That means once you fix the half-block values entering a round, the
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  key is *determined*, not searched. Use meet-in-the-middle on
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  the two middle halves across MANY pairs, not a brute force over keys.

Concr
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ete plan (this is the standard FEAL-4 break):
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 

1. Per pair, from PT compute `L0, R0' = R0
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ⊕L0`. From CT compute `R4 = left(CT)`, `L4 = right(CT)⊕left(CT)`.
2
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] . Guess **K0 only** (2^20). For every pair, K0 fixes `R1 = L
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 0 ⊕ F(R0'⊕K0)` and `L1 = R0'`. Likewise guess **K3 only** (2^20): K3 fixes `R3 = L4`
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] , `L3 = R4 ⊕ F(L4⊕K3)`, giving the state entering round 2 from the back.
3. Now the in
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ner two rounds connect `(L1,R1)` to `(L3,R3)`. The relation `R1 ⊕ R3 =
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  F(L1⊕K1) ⊕ ...` — derive the exact two-equation linear
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] -in-F relation. The crucial trick: there is a relation that depends only on K
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 0 and K3 (not K1,K2) across a pair, e.g. an XOR of intermediate hal
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ves that must match. Find an equation of form `something(K0,
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  pair) = something(K3, pair)` that holds for ALL pairs simultaneously.
4. Build a h
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ash table keyed on the left side (over 2^20 K0 candidates,
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  using a few pairs as a fingerprint) and look up the right side (2^20 K3 candidates). This is 2^20 + 2^
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 20 work, not 2^40. Use 3–4 pairs concatenated as the hash key to make the match unique.
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 
5. Once K0 and K3 are found, K1 and K2 fall out directly by `K1 = (L1)
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  ⊕ F_inv(R1 ⊕ R2)` style inversions — no search.

So: derive the precise intermediate equ
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ations on paper first (re-trace the 4 rounds carefully; you already did most of it), confirm which
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  combination of intermediate halves is independent of K1/K2, then do the MITM keyed on multiple pairs.
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 

Practical notes before you run anything:
- Your current `fast_attack` has a 2^60 loop. Kill it now
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  (`C-c` / pkill); it will only burn the
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  120s timeout.
- Verify each new key-recovery idea against ONE pair using
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  the known-good `feal` binary before scaling up. You have
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  a working test vector already.
- Validate the final keys by re-encrypting all 32 pairs (you do
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  this) AND by running the provided `./decrypt ciphertexts.txt k0 k1 k2 k3` and diffing against your `
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] plaintexts.txt` — that's the authoritative check using their own code.
- Watch correctness details
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] : `expand` is non-injective, so report the recovered *expanded* round keys; when
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  you need a 20-bit seed for the `decrypt` binary, any preimage works. Conf
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] irm at least one preimage exists for each recovered expanded key.
- Remember the cipher takes raw `
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] %lu` decimal in the files; keep 64-bit unsigned form
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] atting consistent.
- If you'd rather avoid the algebra, a clean 2^40 MITM (hash all
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  K0-derived `R1` for one pair, then loop K3 and a single in
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ner key) is fine in C — but DON'T triple-nest 2^20 loops.

Immediate action: stop the running
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  job, write out the round equations explicitly, and confirm which intermediate quantity is K1
[tr-stream call-0039:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] /K2-independent. Then implement the 2^20+2^20 hash-join.
